## 7) Final deliverable summary

### Top 10 architectural strengths

1. Modular directory separation (data/features/models/execution).
2. Presence of telemetry subsystem with API routes.
3. Multiple runtime configs/runs tracked for reproducibility attempts.
4. Dedicated risk and portfolio modules.
5. Frontend and backend separation.
6. Legacy snapshots preserved for auditability.
7. Use of SQL migration for telemetry schema.
8. Data lake organization by raw/cached/manifests.
9. Broad test corpus in backend/deprecated tests.
10. Numerous orchestration scripts for operations.
### Top 10 architectural risks

1. Large volume of legacy/deprecated code increases cognitive load.
2. Potentially stale tracked node_modules content introduces repo noise.
3. Many scripts imply fragmented entrypoints and inconsistent control paths.
4. Static analysis reveals many unknown contracts and implicit assumptions.
5. Potential duplicated logic across backend/algaie/deprecated trees.
6. Config sprawl across TOML/JSON/YAML and runtime folders.
7. Data and code co-located in same repo impacts maintainability.
8. Unclear centralized error/retry policy.
9. Unknown consistent schema versioning across artifacts.
10. Live execution sharp edges due to mixed legacy/new flows.
### 90-day refactor roadmap

- **Phase 1 (0-30 days):** freeze interfaces, define canonical entrypoints, archive deprecated runtime paths behind explicit flags.
- **Phase 2 (31-60 days):** consolidate config loading/versioning, unify telemetry contracts, remove duplicated feature/train pipelines.
- **Phase 3 (61-90 days):** harden live execution with deterministic replay, typed schemas, end-to-end integration tests, and deployment runbooks.
